<a href="/wiki/Mozambican_War_of_Independence" title="Mozambican War of Independence">Mozambique</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>The <b>Portuguese Empire</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Imp&#233;rio Portugu&#234;s</i>), also known as the <b>Portuguese Overseas</b> (<i>Ultramar Portugu&#234;s</i>) or the <b>Portuguese Colonial Empire</b> (<i>Imp&#233;rio Colonial Portugu&#234;s</i>), was one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires"> largest and longest-lived empires</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_history" title="World history">world history</a>. It existed for almost six centuries, from the capture of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> in 1415, to the handover of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Portuguese Macau</a> to <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in 1999. The empire began in the 15th century, and from the early 16th century it stretched across the globe, with bases in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire#Canada" title="Portuguese Empire">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire#Brazil" title="Portuguese Empire">South America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire#Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Portuguese Empire">Africa</a>, and various regions of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire#Goa,_Malacca_and_Southeast_Asia" title="Portuguese Empire">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire#Spice_Islands_(Moluccas)_and_Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Portuguese Empire">Oceania</a>. The Portuguese Empire has been described as the first global empire in history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> a description also given to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Portuguese Empire originated at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, and the power and influence of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a> would eventually expand across the globe. In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries"> Portuguese sailors began exploring</a> the coast of Africa and the Atlantic archipelagos in 1418&#8211;19, using recent developments in navigation, cartography and maritime technology such as the <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravel</a>, with the aim of finding a sea route to the source of the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade"> spice-trade</a>. In 1488 <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> rounded the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, and in 1498 <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> reached India. In 1500, either by an accidental landfall or by the crown\'s secret design, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro &#193;lvares Cabral">Pedro &#193;lvares Cabral</a> discovered Brazil on the South American coast.\n</p><p>Over the following decades, Portuguese sailors continued to explore the coasts and islands of East Asia, establishing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_colonial_forts" title="List of Portuguese colonial forts"> forts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)#Portuguese_Feitorias_(c._1445)" title="Factory (trading post)"> factories</a> as they went. By 1571 a string of naval outposts connected <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a> along the coasts of Africa, the Middle East, India and South Asia. This commercial network and the colonial trade had a substantial positive impact on Portuguese economic growth (1500&#8211;1800), when it accounted for about a fifth of Portugal\'s per-capita income.\n</p><p>When King <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> (Philip I of Portugal) inherited the Portuguese crown in 1580 there began a 60-year union between Spain and Portugal known to subsequent <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>. The realms continued to have separate administrations. As the King of Spain was also King of Portugal, Portuguese colonies became the subject of attacks by three rival European powers hostile to Spain: the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">England</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire"> France</a>. With its smaller population, Portugal found itself unable to effectively defend its overstretched network of trading posts, and the empire began a long and gradual decline. Eventually, Brazil became the most valuable colony of the second era of empire (1663&#8211;1825), until, as part of the wave of <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas"> independence movements</a> that swept the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> during the early 19th century, it broke away in 1822.\n</p><p>The third era of empire covers the final stage of Portuguese colonialism after the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a> in the 1820s. By then, the colonial possessions had been reduced to <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Africa" title="Portuguese Africa">forts and plantations along the African coastline</a> (expanded inland during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a> in the late 19th century), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave"> enclaves</a> in India (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a>) and China (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Portuguese Macau</a>). The <a href="/wiki/1890_British_Ultimatum" title="1890 British Ultimatum">1890 British Ultimatum</a> led to the contraction of <a href="/wiki/Pink_Map" title="Pink Map"> Portuguese ambitions in Africa</a>.\n</p><p>Under <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant&#243;nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant&#243;nio Salazar</a> (in office 1932&#8211;1968), the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Second Portuguese Republic</a> made some ill-fated attempts to cling on to its last remaining colonies. Under the ideology of <a href="/wiki/Pluricontinentalism" title="Pluricontinentalism">Pluricontinentalism</a>, the regime renamed its colonies "<a href="/wiki/Overseas_province" title="Overseas province">overseas provinces</a>" while retaining the <a href="/wiki/Chibalo" title="Chibalo">system of forced labour</a>, from which only a small <a href="/wiki/Assimilado" title="Assimilado">indigenous &#233;lite</a> was normally exempt. In 1961 India <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Goa" title="Annexation of Goa"> annexed Goa</a> and Dahomey (now Benin) annexed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_of_S%C3%A3o_Jo%C3%A3o_Baptista_de_Ajud%C3%A1" title="Fort of S&#227;o Jo&#227;o Baptista de Ajud&#225;">Fort of S&#227;o Jo&#227;o Baptista de Ajud&#225;</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> in Africa lasted from 1961 until the final overthrow of the Estado Novo regime in 1974. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> of April 1974 in Lisbon led to the hasty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Africa" title="Decolonization of Africa"> decolonization of Portuguese Africa</a> and to the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor"> 1975 annexation of Portuguese Timor</a> by Indonesia. Decolonization prompted the exodus of nearly all the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retornados" title="Retornados"> Portuguese colonial settlers</a> and of many <a href="/wiki/Luso-Africans" title="Luso-Africans">mixed-race people</a> from the colonies. Portugal <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Macau" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Macau">returned</a> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau"> Macau</a> to China in 1999. The only overseas possessions to remain under Portuguese rule, <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous Regions of Portugal">the Azores and Madeira</a>, both had overwhelmingly <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people"> Portuguese populations</a>, and Lisbon subsequently changed their <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_the_Azores" title="Political status of the Azores"> constitutional status</a> from "<a href="/wiki/Overseas_province" title="Overseas province">overseas provinces</a>" to "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions" title="Autonomous regions">autonomous regions</a>".\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span id="Background_.281139.E2.80.931415.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_(1139&#8211;1415)">Background (1139&#8211;1415)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background (1139&#8211;1415)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1139%E2%80%931415)" title="History of Portugal (1139&#8211;1415)">History of Portugal (1139&#8211;1415)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta,_s.XV.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1926" data-file-width="2937" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG/220px-Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG/330px-Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG/440px-Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta%2C_s.XV.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Infante_D._Henrique_na_conquista_de_Ceuta,_s.XV.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Ceuta" title="Conquest of Ceuta">Conquest of Ceuta</a>, in 1415, was led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, and initiated the Portuguese Empire.</div></div></div>\n<p>The origin of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a> lay in the <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">reconquista</a></i>, the gradual reconquest of the Iberian peninsula from the <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Moors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius301_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius301-6">[6]</a></sup> After establishing itself as a separate kingdom in 1139, Portugal completed its reconquest of Moorish territory by reaching <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> in 1249, but its independence continued to be threatened by neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> until the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ayll%C3%B3n" title="Treaty of Ayll&#243;n">Treaty of Ayll&#243;n</a> in 1411.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt2005p15-17_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt2005p15-17-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Free from threats to its existence and unchallenged by the wars fought by other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_states" title="European states">European states</a>, Portuguese attention turned overseas and towards a military expedition to the Muslim lands of North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt19_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt19-8">[8]</a></sup> There were several probable motives for their first attack, on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinid_Dynasty" title="Marinid Dynasty">Marinid Sultanate</a> (in present-day <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>). It offered the opportunity to continue the Christian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusade" title="Crusade">crusade</a> against <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>; to the military class, it promised glory on the battlefield and the spoils of war;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer19_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer19-9">[9]</a></sup> and finally, it was also a chance to expand Portuguese trade and to address Portugal\'s economic decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt19_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt19-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1415 an attack was made on <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, a strategically located North African Muslim enclave along the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, and one of the terminal ports of the trans-Saharan gold and slave trades. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ceuta" title="Battle of Ceuta">conquest</a> was a military success, and marked one of the first steps in Portuguese expansion beyond the Iberian Peninsula,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> but it proved costly to defend against the Muslim forces that soon besieged it. The Portuguese were unable to use it as a base for further expansion into the hinterland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt21_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt21-11">[11]</a></sup> and the trans-Saharan caravans merely shifted their routes to bypass Ceuta and/or used alternative Muslim ports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius55_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius55-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="First_era_.281415.E2.80.931663.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_era_(1415&#8211;1663)">First era (1415&#8211;1663)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First era (1415&#8211;1663)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PortugueseFlag1485.svg"><img alt="PortugueseFlag1485.svg" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="170" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">Prehistoric Iberia</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman Peoples</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Roman conquest of Hispania">Roman conquest of Hispania</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Hispania" title="Romanization of Hispania">Romanization of Hispania</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Suebic Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal#Moorish_rule_and_the_Reconquista_(711&#8211;1249)" title="History of Portugal">Medieval</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal#The_First_Republic_(1910&#8211;1926)" title="History of Portugal">First Republic</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/First_Portuguese_Republic" title="First Portuguese d\'&#233;tat</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" War</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" Republic</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Processo_Revolucion%C3%A1rio_Em_Curso" title="Processo Revolucion&#225;rio Em Curso">Processo Revolucion&#225;rio Em Curso</a></i></li>\n<li><a Republic">Third Republic</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal" title="History of Portugal">Topic</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Category:Archives_in_Portugal" title="Category:Archives in Portugal">Archives</a> - <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">Economy</a> - <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portuguese" title="History of Portuguese">Language</a> - <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Portugal" title="Military history of Portugal">Military</a> - <a href="/wiki/Music_history_of_Portugal" title="Music history of Portugal">Music</a></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#eee; text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous Regions of Portugal">Regions</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Azores" title="History of the Azores">Azorean history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_Madeira" title="History of Madeira">Madeiran history</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><th style="padding:0.1em">\n<a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Portuguese_history" title="Timeline of Portuguese history">Timeline</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;border-top:1px solid #ccc; border-bottom:1px solid #ccc">\n<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Portugal.svg"><img alt="Flag of Portugal.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/16px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/24px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/32px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Portugal" title="Portal:Portugal">Portugal portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Portugal" title="Template:History of Portugal"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Portugal" title="Template talk:History of Portugal"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Portugal&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415%E2%80%931578)" title="History of Portugal (1415&#8211;1578)">History of Portugal (1415&#8211;1578)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese discoveries</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_enclaves_in_North_Africa_before_1830" title="European enclaves in North Africa before 1830">European enclaves in North Africa before 1830</a></div>\n<p>Although Ceuta proved to be a disappointment for the Portuguese, the decision was taken to hold it while exploring along the Atlantic African coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius55_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius55-12">[12]</a></sup> A key supporter of this policy was <a href="/wiki/Infante" title="Infante">Infante</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dom_(title)" title="Dom (title)">Dom</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, who had been involved in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ceuta" title="Battle of Ceuta">capture of Ceuta</a>, and who took the lead role in promoting and financing Portuguese maritime exploration until his death in 1460.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius56_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius56-13">[13]</a></sup> At the time, Europeans did not know what lay beyond <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bojador" title="Cape Bojador">Cape Bojador</a> on the African coast. Henry wished to know how far the Muslim territories in Africa extended, and whether it was possible to reach Asia by sea, both to reach the source of the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> and perhaps to join forces with the fabled Christian kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Prester_John" title="Prester John">Prester John</a> that was rumoured to exist somewhere in the "Indies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer19_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer19-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson50_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson50-14">[14]</a></sup> Under his sponsorship, soon the Atlantic islands of <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> (1419) and <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> (1427) were reached and started to be settled producing wheat to export to Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coates60_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coates60-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="556" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png/300px-Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png/450px-Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend-line"><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 2em; height: 0px; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted #000; border-top: green solid 2px;">&#160;</span>&#160;P&#234;ro da Covilh&#227; and <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Paiva" title="Afonso de Paiva">Afonso de Paiva</a> common route to <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a> in 1487&#8211;1488 (green);</div> <div class="legend-line"><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 2em; height: 0px; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted #000; border-top: orange solid 2px;">&#160;</span>&#160;Covilh&#227; travel 1489&#8211;&#8224;1490 (orange);</div> <div class="legend-line"><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 2em; height: 0px; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted #000; border-top: blue solid 2px;">&#160;</span>&#160;Covilh&#227; travel to <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> 1490&#8211;&#8224;1530? (blue);</div> <div class="legend-line"><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 2em; height: 0px; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted #000; border-top: black solid 2px;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> travel 1497&#8211;1499 (black)</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The main Portuguese goal was trade, not colonization or conquest. Soon its ships were bringing into the European market highly valued gold, ivory, pepper, cotton, sugar, and slaves. The slave trade, for example, was conducted by a few dozen merchants in Lisbon. In the process of expanding the trade routes, Portuguese navigators mapped unknown parts of Africa, and began exploring the Indian Ocean. In 1487, an overland expedition by <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_da_Covilh%C3%A3" title="P&#234;ro da Covilh&#227;">P&#234;ro da Covilh&#227;</a> made its way to India, exploring trade opportunities with the Indians and Arabs, and winding up finally in Ethiopia. His detailed report was eagerly read in Lisbon, Which became the best informed center for global geography and trade routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_African_coastline_excursions">Initial African coastline excursions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Initial African coastline excursions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fears of what lay beyond <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bojador" title="Cape Bojador">Cape Bojador</a>, and whether it was possible to return once it was passed, were assuaged in 1434 when it was rounded by one of Infante Henry\'s captains, <a href="/wiki/Gil_Eanes" title="Gil Eanes">Gil Eanes</a>. Once this psychological barrier had been crossed, it became easier to probe further along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius68_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius68-17">[17]</a></sup> In 1443 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Pedro,_Duke_of_Coimbra" title="Infante Pedro, Duke of Coimbra">Infante Dom Pedro</a>, Henry\'s brother and by then regent of the Kingdom, granted him the monopoly of navigation, war and trade in the lands south of Cape Bojador. Later this monopoly would be enforced by the <a href="/wiki/Papal_bull" title="Papal bull">papal bulls</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Dum_Diversas" title="Dum Diversas">Dum Diversas</a></i> (1452) and <i><a href="/wiki/Romanus_Pontifex" title="Romanus Pontifex">Romanus Pontifex</a></i> (1455), granting Portugal the trade monopoly for the newly discovered lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daus33_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daus33-18">[18]</a></sup> A major advance that accelerated this project was the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravel</a> in the mid-15th century, a ship that could be sailed closer to the wind than any other in operation in Europe at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer29_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer29-19">[19]</a></sup> Using this new maritime technology, Portuguese navigators reached ever more southerly <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a>, advancing at an average rate of one degree a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russell-Wood1998p9_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Russell-Wood1998p9-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Peninsula" title="Cape Verde Peninsula">Cape Verde Peninsula</a> were reached in 1445.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez79_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez79-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3636" data-file-width="2519" decoding="async" height="361" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg/250px-L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg/375px-L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg/500px-L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L%C3%A1zaro_Luis_1563.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Western Africa by L&#225;zaro Luis (1563). The large castle in West Africa represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_da_Mina" title="S&#227;o Jorge da Mina">S&#227;o Jorge da Mina</a> (Elmina castle).</div></div></div>\n<p>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feitoria" title="Feitoria">feitoria</a> trade post overseas was established in 1445 on the island of <a href="/wiki/Arguin" title="Arguin">Arguin</a>, off the coast of Mauritania, to attract Muslim traders and monopolize the business in the routes travelled in North Africa. In 1446, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Fernandes" title="&#193;lvaro Fernandes">&#193;lvaro Fernandes</a> pushed on almost as far as present-day <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> was reached in the 1460s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius469_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius469-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> Islands were discovered in 1456 and settled in 1462.\n</p><p>Expansion of <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> in Madeira started in 1455, using advisers from <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and (largely) <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> capital to produce the <i>"sweet salt"</i> <a href="/wiki/History_of_sugar" title="History of sugar">rare in Europe</a>. Already cultivated in <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>, the accessibility of Madeira attracted Genoese and Flemish traders keen to bypass Venetian monopolies. Slaves were used, and the proportion of imported slaves in Madeira reached 10% of the total population by the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> By 1480 <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> had some seventy ships engaged in the Madeira sugar trade, with the refining and distribution concentrated in Antwerp. By the 1490s Madeira had overtaken Cyprus as a producer of sugar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponting482_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ponting482-24">[24]</a></sup> The success of sugar merchants such as <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeo_Marchionni" title="Bartolomeo Marchionni">Bartolomeo Marchionni</a> would propel the investment in future travels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis84_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis84-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1469, after prince Henry\'s death and as a result of meagre returns of the African explorations, King <a href="/wiki/Afonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Afonso V of Portugal">Afonso V</a> granted the monopoly of trade in part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> to merchant <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes" title="Fern&#227;o Gomes">Fern&#227;o Gomes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto232_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto232-26">[26]</a></sup> Gomes, who had to explore 100 miles (160&#160;km) of the coast each year for five years, discovered the islands of the Gulf of Guinea, including <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe">S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe</a> and found a thriving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alluvial" title="Alluvial">alluvial</a> gold trade among the natives and visiting Arab and Berber traders at the port then named <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">Mina</a> (the mine), where he established a trading post.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White138_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-White138-27">[27]</a></sup> Trade between Elmina and Portugal grew throughout a decade. In 1481, the recently crowned <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">Jo&#227;o II</a> decided to build <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_da_Mina" title="S&#227;o Jorge da Mina">S&#227;o Jorge da Mina</a> in order to ensure the protection of this trade, which was held again as a royal monopoly. The <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a> was crossed by navigators sponsored by Fern&#227;o Gomes in 1473 and the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> by <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo C&#227;o">Diogo C&#227;o</a> in 1482. It was during this expedition that the Portuguese first encountered the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>, with which it soon developed a rapport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GannDuignan273_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-GannDuignan273-28">[28]</a></sup> During his 1485&#8211;86 expedition, C&#227;o continued to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cross" title="Cape Cross">Cape Cross</a>, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius156_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius156-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Morocco.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="586" decoding="async" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Portuguese_Morocco.PNG/300px-Portuguese_Morocco.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Portuguese_Morocco.PNG/450px-Portuguese_Morocco.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/Portuguese_Morocco.PNG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Morocco.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Morocco%E2%80%93Portugal_relations" title="Morocco&#8211;Portugal relations">Portuguese possessions in Morocco</a> (1415&#8211;1769)</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1488, <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> rounded the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> on the southern tip of Africa, proving false the view that had existed since <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> that the Indian Ocean was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land-locked" title="Land-locked">land-locked</a>. Simultaneously <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_da_Covilh%C3%A3" title="P&#234;ro da Covilh&#227;">P&#234;ro da Covilh&#227;</a>, traveling secretly overland, had reached <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, suggesting that a sea route to the Indies would soon be forthcoming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson59_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson59-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the Portuguese explored the coastlines of Africa, they left behind a series of <a href="/wiki/Padr%C3%A3o" title="Padr&#227;o">padr&#245;es</a>, stone crosses engraved with the Portuguese coat of arms marking their claims,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt47_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt47-31">[31]</a></sup> and built forts and trading posts. From these bases, they engaged profitably in the slave and gold trades. Portugal enjoyed a virtual monopoly on the African seaborne slave trade for over a century, importing around 800 slaves annually. Most were brought to the Portuguese capital <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, where it is estimated black Africans came to constitute 10 percent of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson55_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson55-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Treaty_of_Tordesillas_.281494.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Tordesillas_(1494)">Treaty of Tordesillas (1494)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Treaty of Tordesillas (1494)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spain_and_Portugal.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="771" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Spain_and_Portugal.png/300px-Spain_and_Portugal.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Spain_and_Portugal.png/450px-Spain_and_Portugal.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Spain_and_Portugal.png/600px-Spain_and_Portugal.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spain_and_Portugal.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1494 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a> meridian divided the world between the crowns <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">of Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">of Castile</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1492 <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>\'s after-discovery for Spain of the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, which he believed to be Asia, led to disputes between the Spanish and Portuguese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McAlister73-75_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-McAlister73-75-33">[33]</a></sup> These were eventually settled by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a> in 1494, which divided the world outside of Europe in an exclusive <a href="/wiki/Duopoly" title="Duopoly">duopoly</a> between the Portuguese and the Spanish along a north-south meridian 370 <a href="/wiki/League_(unit)" title="League (unit)">leagues</a>, or 970 miles (1,560&#160;km), west of the Cape Verde islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto165_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto165-34">[34]</a></sup> However, as it was not possible at the time to correctly measure <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a>, the exact boundary was disputed by the two countries until 1777.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius174_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius174-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The completion of these negotiations with Spain is one of several reasons proposed by historians for why it took nine years for the Portuguese to follow up on Dias\'s voyage to the Cape of Good Hope, though it has also been speculated that other voyages were in fact taking place in secret during this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius176_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius176-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer36_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer36-37">[37]</a></sup> Whether or not this was the case, the long-standing Portuguese goal of finding a sea route to Asia was finally achieved in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discovery_of_the_sea_route_to_India" title="Discovery of the sea route to India">ground-breaking voyage</a> commanded by <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius176-185_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius176-185-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_enter_the_Indian_Ocean">Portuguese enter the Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Portuguese enter the Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">Portuguese India Armadas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1224" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg/220px-A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg/330px-A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg/440px-A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_partida_de_Vasco_da_Gama_para_a_%C3%8Dndia_em_1497.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>\'s departure to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, in 1497</div></div></div>\n<p>The squadron of <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> left Portugal in 1497, rounded the Cape and continued along the coast of East Africa, where a local pilot was brought on board who guided them across the Indian Ocean, reaching <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Calicut</a> (the capital of the native kingdom ruled by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zamorin" title="Zamorin">Zamorins</a> (This city also known as <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Kozhikode</a>) in south-western India in May 1498.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The second voyage to India was dispatched in 1500 under <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro &#193;lvares Cabral">Pedro &#193;lvares Cabral</a>. While following the same south-westerly route as Gama across the Atlantic Ocean, Cabral made landfall on the Brazilian coast. This was probably an accidental discovery, but it has been speculated that the Portuguese secretly knew of Brazil\'s existence and that it lay on their side of the Tordesillas line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McAlister75_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-McAlister75-40">[40]</a></sup> Cabral recommended to the Portuguese King that the land be settled, and two follow up voyages were sent in 1501 and 1503. The land was found to be abundant in <i><a href="/wiki/Paubrasilia" title="Paubrasilia">pau-brasil</a></i>, or brazilwood, from which it later inherited its name, but the failure to find gold or silver meant that for the time being Portuguese efforts were concentrated on India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McAlister76_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-McAlister76-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1502, to enforce its trade monopoly over a wide area of the Indian Ocean, the Portuguese Empire created the <a href="/wiki/Cartaz" title="Cartaz">cartaz</a> licensing system, granting merchant ships protection against pirates and rival states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius274,320-323_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius274,320-323-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/300px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/450px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/600px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese discoveries</a> and explorations: first arrival places and dates; main Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> routes (blue)</div></div></div>\n<p>Profiting from the rivalry between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochin_kingdom" title="Cochin kingdom">ruler of Kochi</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zamorin" title="Zamorin">Zamorin</a> of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kozhikode" title="History of Kozhikode">Calicut</a>, the Portuguese were well-received and seen as allies, as they obtained a permit to build the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Emmanuel" title="Fort Emmanuel">fort <i>Immanuel</i></a> (<a href="/wiki/Fort_Kochi" title="Fort Kochi">Fort Kochi</a>) and a trading post that were the first European settlement in India. They established a trading center at <a href="/wiki/Tangasseri" title="Tangasseri">Tangasseri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quilon" title="Quilon">Quilon</a> (<i>Coul&#227;o</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kollam" title="Kollam">Kollam</a>) city in (1503) in 1502, which became the centre of trade in pepper,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and after founding manufactories at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochin" title="Cochin">Cochin</a> (<i>Cochim</i>, Kochi) and <a href="/wiki/Kannur" title="Kannur">Cannanore</a> (<i>Canonor</i>, Kannur), built a factory at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quilon" title="Quilon">Quilon</a> in 1503. In 1505 King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> appointed <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Francisco de Almeida</a> first <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">Viceroy</a> of Portuguese India, establishing the Portuguese government in the east. That year the Portuguese also conquered <a href="/wiki/Kannur" title="Kannur">Kannur</a>, where they founded <a href="/wiki/St._Angelo_Fort" title="St. Angelo Fort">St. Angelo Fort</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Louren%C3%A7o_de_Almeida" title="Louren&#231;o de Almeida">Louren&#231;o de Almeida</a> arrived in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a> (modern Sri Lanka), where he discovered the source of <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto207_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto207-44">[44]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Cankili_I" title="Cankili I">Cankili I</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jaffna" title="Jaffna">Jaffna</a> initially resisted contact with them, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaffna_kingdom" title="Jaffna kingdom">Jaffna kingdom</a> came to the attention of Portuguese officials soon after for their resistance to missionary activities as well as logistical reasons due to its proximity with <a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a> harbour among other reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abeyasinghe2_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abeyasinghe2-45">[45]</a></sup> In the same year, Manuel I ordered Almeida to fortify the Portuguese fortresses in Kerala and within eastern Africa, as well as probe into the prospects of building forts in Sri Lanka and Malacca in response to growing hostilities with Muslims within those regions and threats from the Mamluk sultan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b128_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b128-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1297" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg/220px-Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg/330px-Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg/440px-Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Carracks_off_a_Rocky_Coast.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_do_Monte_Sinai" title="Santa Catarina do Monte Sinai">Santa Catarina do Monte Sinai</a> carrack exemplified the might and the force of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Portuguese Armada</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1331" data-file-width="1872" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg/220px-Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg/330px-Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg/440px-Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Codice_Casanatense_Portuguese_Nobleman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>16th century Portuguese illustration from the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3dice_Casanatense" title="C&#243;dice Casanatense">C&#243;dice Casanatense</a>, depicting a Portuguese nobleman with his retinue in India</div></div></div>\n<p>A Portuguese fleet under the command of <a href="/wiki/Trist%C3%A3o_da_Cunha" title="Trist&#227;o da Cunha">Trist&#227;o da Cunha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> conquered <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">Socotra</a> at the entrance of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> in 1506 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a> in 1507. Having failed to conquer <a href="/wiki/Ormus" title="Ormus">Ormuz</a>, they instead followed a strategy intended to close off commerce to and from the Indian Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius233,235_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius233,235-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> was partly explored by Cunha, and <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> was discovered by Cunha whilst possibly being accompanied by Albuquerque.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macmillan11_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macmillan11-48">[48]</a></sup> After the capture of Socotra, Cunha and Albuquerque operated separately. While Cunha traveled India and Portugal for trading purposes, Albuquerque went to India to take over as governor after Almeida\'s three-year term ended. Almeida refused to turn over power and soon placed Albuquerque under house arrest, where he remained until 1509.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius237-239_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius237-239-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although requested by Manuel I to further explore interests in Malacca and Sri Lanka, Almeida instead focused on western India, in particular the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Gujarat" title="Sultanate of Gujarat">Sultanate of Gujarat</a> due to his suspicions of traders from the region possessing more power. The <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Maml&#251;k Sultanate</a> sultan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Ashraf_Qansuh_al-Ghawri" title="Al-Ashraf Qansuh al-Ghawri">Al-Ashraf Qansuh al-Ghawri</a> along with the Gujarati sultanate attacked Portuguese forces in the harbor of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chaul" title="Battle of Chaul">Chaul</a>, resulting in the death of <a href="/wiki/Louren%C3%A7o_de_Almeida" title="Louren&#231;o de Almeida">Almeida\'s son</a>. In retaliation, the Portuguese fought and destroyed the Mamluks and Gujarati fleets in the sea <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Diu_(1509)" title="Battle of Diu (1509)">Battle of Diu</a> in 1509.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b128-29_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b128-29-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with Almeida\'s initial attempts, Manuel I and his council in Lisbon had tried to distribute power in the Indian Ocean, creating three areas of jurisdiction: Albuquerque was sent to the Red Sea, <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Lopes_de_Sequeira" title="Diogo Lopes de Sequeira">Diogo Lopes de Sequeira</a> to South-east Asia, seeking an agreement with the Sultan of Malacca, and Jorge de Aguiar followed by Duarte de Lemos were sent to the area between the Cape of Good Hope and Gujarat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius245-247_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius245-247-51">[51]</a></sup> However, such posts were centralized by Afonso de Albuquerque after his succession and remained so in subsequent ruling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Subrahmanyam67-83_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Subrahmanyam67-83-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Trade_with_Maritime_Asia.2C_Africa_and_the_Indian_Ocean"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_with_Maritime_Asia,_Africa_and_the_Indian_Ocean">Trade with Maritime Asia, Africa and the Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Trade with Maritime Asia, Africa and the Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Macau" title="History of Macau">History of Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Goa" title="History of Goa">History of Goa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Malacca" title="Portuguese Malacca">Portuguese Malacca</a></div>\n<h4><span id="Goa.2C_Malacca_and_Southeast_Asia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Goa,_Malacca_and_Southeast_Asia">Goa, Malacca and Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Goa, Malacca and Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="1113" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg/300px-Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg/450px-Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg/600px-Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asia_oceania_anonymous_c1550.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the 16th and 17th centuries, the Portuguese Empire of the East, or <i>Estado da &#205;ndia</i> ("State of India"), with its capital in Goa, included possessions (as subjected areas with a certain degree of autonomy) in all the Asian sub-continents, East Africa, and Pacific.</div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of 1509, Albuquerque became viceroy of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estado_da_%C3%8Dndia" title="Estado da &#205;ndia">Portuguese India</a>. In contrast to Almeida, Albuquerque was more concerned with strengthening the navy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b129_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b129-53">[53]</a></sup> as well as being more compliant with the interests of the kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius238_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius238-54">[54]</a></sup> His first objective was to conquer Goa, due to its strategic location as a defensive fort positioned between Kerala and Gujarat, as well as its prominence for <a href="/wiki/Arabian_horse" title="Arabian horse">Arabian horse</a> imports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b128-29_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b128-29-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Conquest_of_Goa_(1510)" title="Portuguese Conquest of Goa (1510)">The initial capture of Goa</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Adil_Shahi_dynasty" title="Adil Shahi dynasty">Bijapur sultanate</a> in 1510 was soon countered by the Bijapuris, but with the help of Hindu <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateer</a> <a href="/wiki/Timoji" title="Timoji">Timoji</a>, on November 25 of the same year it was recaptured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shastry34-45_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shastry34-45-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b130_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b130-56">[56]</a></sup> In Goa, Albuquerque began the first Portuguese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mint_(coin)" title="Mint (coin)">mint</a> in India in 1510.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deSouza220_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-deSouza220-57">[57]</a></sup> He encouraged Portuguese settlers to marry local women, built a church in honor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="St. Catherine of Alexandria">St. Catherine</a> (as it was recaptured on her feast day), and attempted to build rapport with the Hindus by protecting their temples and reducing their tax requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b130_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b130-56">[56]</a></sup> The Portuguese maintained friendly relations with the south Indian Emperors of the <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mehta291_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mehta291-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 1511 Albuquerque sailed to <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a> in Malaysia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ricklefs23_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ricklefs23-59">[59]</a></sup> the largest spice market of the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kratoska2004p98_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kratoska2004p98-60">[60]</a></sup> Though the trade was largely dominated by the Gujurati, other groups such as the Turks, Persians, Armenians, Tamils and <a href="/wiki/People_of_Ethiopia" title="People of Ethiopia">Abyssinians</a> traded there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kratoska2004p98_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kratoska2004p98-60">[60]</a></sup> Albuquerque targeted Malacca to impede the Muslim and Venetian influence in the spice trade and increase that of Lisbon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gipouloux2011p301-302_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gipouloux2011p301-302-61">[61]</a></sup> By July 1511, Albuquerque had captured Malacca and sent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Abreu" title="Antonio de Abreu">Antonio de Abreu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serr&#227;o">Francisco Serr&#227;o</a> (along with Ferdinand Magellan) to explore the Indonesian archipelago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt2005p78_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt2005p78-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="956" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg/220px-Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg/330px-Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg/440px-Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iberian_mare_clausum_claims.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iberian \'mare clausum\' in the Age of Discovery. Afonso de Albuquerque\'s strategy to encircle the Indian Ocean is shown.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Malacca peninsula became the strategic base for Portuguese trade expansion with China and Southeast Asia. A strong gate, called the <a href="/wiki/A_Famosa" title="A Famosa">A Famosa</a>, was erected to defend the city and still remains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ooi2009p202_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi2009p202-63">[63]</a></sup> Learning of Siamese ambitions over Malacca, Albuquerque immediately sent <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Fernandes" title="Duarte Fernandes">Duarte Fernandes</a> on a diplomatic mission to the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Kingdom of Siam</a> (modern Thailand), where he was the first European to arrive, establishing amicable relations and trade between both kingdoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lach520-521_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lach520-521-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Portuguese empire pushed further south and proceeded to discover Timor in 1512. <a href="/wiki/Jorge_de_Menezes" title="Jorge de Menezes">Jorge de Meneses</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> in 1526, naming it the "Island of the Papua".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuanchiRobson2005_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-QuanchiRobson2005-66">[66]</a></sup> In 1517, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_da_Silveira" title="Jo&#227;o da Silveira">Jo&#227;o da Silveira</a> commanded a fleet to <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and by 1528, the Portuguese had established a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_settlement_in_Chittagong" title="Portuguese settlement in Chittagong">settlement in Chittagong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harris225_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harris225-68">[68]</a></sup> The Portuguese eventually based their center of operations along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugli_River" title="Hugli River">Hugli River</a>, where they encountered Muslims, Hindus, and Portuguese deserters known as <i>Chatins</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="China_and_Japan">China and Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: China and Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Portugal" title="Chinese people in Portugal">Chinese people in Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">Nanban trade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Portugal" title="Slavery in Portugal">Slavery in Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Nagasaki" title="Portuguese Nagasaki">Portuguese Nagasaki</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Trade_Routes.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Macau_Trade_Routes.png/300px-Macau_Trade_Routes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Macau_Trade_Routes.png/450px-Macau_Trade_Routes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Macau_Trade_Routes.png/600px-Macau_Trade_Routes.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Trade_Routes.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Portuguese founded the city of <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki, Japan</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Jorge Alvares was the first European to reach China by sea, while the Romans were the first overland via Asia Minor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edmonds2002_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edmonds2002-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward2008_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ward2008-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleason2007_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gleason2007-73">[73]</a></sup> He was also the first European to discover Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In 1514, Afonso de Albuquerque, the Viceroy of the Estado da India, dispatched Italian Rafael Perestrello to sail to China in order to pioneer European trade relations with the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In spite of initial harmony and excitement between the two cultures, difficulties began to arise shortly afterwards, including misunderstanding, bigotry, and even hostility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smithsonianmag.com_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-smithsonianmag.com-78">[78]</a></sup> The Portuguese explorer Sim&#227;o de Andrade incited poor relations with China due to his pirate activities, raiding Chinese shipping, attacking a Chinese official, and kidnappings of Chinese. He based himself at Tamao island in a fort. The Chinese claimed that Sim&#227;o kidnapped Chinese boys and girls to be molested and cannibalized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jesus5_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jesus5-79">[79]</a></sup> The Chinese sent a squadron of junks against Portuguese caravels that succeeded in driving the Portuguese away and reclaiming Tamao. As a result, the Chinese posted an edict banning men with caucasian features from entering Canton, killing multiple Portuguese there, and driving the Portuguese back to sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dodge226_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dodge226-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whiteway339_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whiteway339-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_oldmap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="552" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Macau_oldmap.jpg/220px-Macau_oldmap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Macau_oldmap.jpg/330px-Macau_oldmap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Macau_oldmap.jpg/440px-Macau_oldmap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_oldmap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A depiction, from 1639, of the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Peninsula" title="Macau Peninsula">Macau Peninsula</a>, during the golden age of colonization of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Portuguese Macau</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Sultan of Bintan detained several Portuguese under Tom&#225;s Pires, the Chinese then executed 23 Portuguese and threw the rest into prison where they resided in squalid, sometimes fatal conditions. The Chinese then massacred Portuguese who resided at <a href="/wiki/Ningbo" title="Ningbo">Ningbo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> trading posts in 1545 and 1549, due to extensive and damaging raids by the Portuguese along the coast, which irritated the Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dodge226_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dodge226-80">[80]</a></sup> Portuguese pirating was second to Japanese pirating by this period. However, they soon began to shield Chinese junks and a cautious trade began. In 1557 the Chinese authorities allowed the Portuguese to settle in Macau, creating a warehouse in the trade of goods between China, Japan, Goa and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dodge226_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dodge226-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b175,184_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b175,184-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Spice_Islands_.28Moluccas.29_and_Treaty_of_Zaragoza"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spice_Islands_(Moluccas)_and_Treaty_of_Zaragoza">Spice Islands (Moluccas) and Treaty of Zaragoza</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Spice Islands (Moluccas) and Treaty of Zaragoza">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NanbanCarrack.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="958" data-file-width="1038" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/NanbanCarrack.jpg/220px-NanbanCarrack.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/NanbanCarrack.jpg/330px-NanbanCarrack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/NanbanCarrack.jpg/440px-NanbanCarrack.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NanbanCarrack.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portugal was the first European nation to <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">establish trade routes with Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Fern&#227;o Pires de Andrade">China</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Portuguese operations in Asia did not go unnoticed, and in 1521 <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Magellan</a> arrived in the region and claimed the Philippines for Spain. In 1525, Spain under Charles V sent an expedition to colonize the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moluccas_islands" title="Moluccas islands">Moluccas islands</a>, claiming they were in his zone of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, since there was no set limit to the east. The expedition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garc%C3%ADa_Jofre_de_Loa%C3%ADsa" title="Garc&#237;a Jofre de Loa&#237;sa">Garc&#237;a Jofre de Loa&#237;sa</a> reached the Moluccas, docking at <a href="/wiki/Tidore" title="Tidore">Tidore</a>. With the Portuguese already established in nearby Ternate, conflict was inevitable, leading to nearly a decade of skirmishes. A resolution was reached with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Treaty of Zaragoza">Treaty of Zaragoza</a> in 1529, attributing the Moluccas to Portugal and the Philippines to Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ooi2004p1340_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi2004p1340-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="South_Asia.2C_Persian_Gulf_and_Red_Sea"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia,_Persian_Gulf_and_Red_Sea">South Asia, Persian Gulf and Red Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: South Asia, Persian Gulf and Red Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Portuguese empire expanded into the Persian Gulf, contesting control of the spice trade with the <a href="/wiki/Ajuran_Sultanate" title="Ajuran Sultanate">Ajuran Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. In 1515, Afonso de Albuquerque <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Ormuz_(1507)" title="Capture of Ormuz (1507)">conquered</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huwala" title="Huwala">Huwala</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Ormus" title="Ormus">Hormuz</a> at the head of the Persian Gulf, establishing it as a vassal state. <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a>, however, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Aden" title="Siege of Aden">resisted</a> Albuquerque\'s expedition in that same year and another attempt by Albuquerque\'s successor <a href="/wiki/Lopo_Soares_de_Albergaria" title="Lopo Soares de Albergaria">Lopo Soares de Albergaria</a> in 1516. In 1521 a force led by <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Correia_(admiral)" title="Ant&#243;nio Correia (admiral)">Ant&#243;nio Correia</a> captured <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, defeating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabrid" title="Jabrid">Jabrid</a> King, <a href="/wiki/Muqrin_ibn_Zamil" title="Muqrin ibn Zamil">Muqrin ibn Zamil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In a shifting series of alliances, the Portuguese dominated much of the southern Persian Gulf for the next hundred years. With the regular maritime route linking Lisbon to Goa since 1497, the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Mozambique" title="Island of Mozambique">island of Mozambique</a> became a strategic port, and there was built <a href="/wiki/Fort_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o" title="Fort S&#227;o Sebasti&#227;o">Fort S&#227;o Sebasti&#227;o</a> and a hospital. In the Azores, the Islands Armada protected the ships en route to Lisbon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O\'Flanagan125_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-O\'Flanagan125-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1534, Gujarat faced attack from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughals" title="Mughals">Mughals</a> and the Rajput states of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chitor" title="Chitor">Chitor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandu,_Madhya_Pradesh" title="Mandu, Madhya Pradesh">Mandu</a>. The Sultan <a href="/wiki/Bahadur_Shah_of_Gujarat" title="Bahadur Shah of Gujarat">Bahadur Shah of Gujarat</a> was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bassein_(1534)" title="Treaty of Bassein (1534)">Treaty of Bassein</a> with the Portuguese, establishing an alliance to regain the country, giving in exchange <a href="/wiki/Daman,_Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman, Daman and Diu">Daman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diu,_India" title="Diu, India">Diu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vasai" title="Vasai">Bassein</a>. It also regulated the trade of Gujarati ships departing to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and passing through Bassein to pay duties and allow the horse trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson1976pp74-82_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson1976pp74-82-86">[86]</a></sup> After Mughal ruler <a href="/wiki/Humayun" title="Humayun">Humayun</a> had success against Bahadur, the latter signed another treaty with the Portuguese to confirm the provisions and allowed the fort to be built in Diu. Shortly afterward, Humayun turned his attention elsewhere, and the Gujarats allied with the Ottomans to regain control of Diu and lay siege to the fort. The two failed sieges of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Diu" title="Siege of Diu">1538</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Siege_of_Diu" title="Second Siege of Diu">1546</a> put an end to Ottoman ambitions, confirming the Portuguese hegemony in the region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson1976pp74-82_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson1976pp74-82-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malekandathil116-118_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malekandathil116-118-87">[87]</a></sup> as well as gaining superiority over the Mughals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mathew138_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mathew138-88">[88]</a></sup> However, the Ottomans fought off attacks from the Portuguese in the Red Sea and in the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Peninsula</a> in 1541, and in the northern region of the Persian Gulf in 1546 and 1552.
