Each entity ultimately had to respect the sphere of influence of the other, albeit unofficially.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-Saharan_Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sub-Saharan Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Theodore_de_Bry_-_Harbour_scene_(colorized).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Theodore_de_Bry_-_Harbour_scene_%28colorized%29.jpg/220px-Theodore_de_Bry_-_Harbour_scene_%28colorized%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/Theodore_de_Bry_-_Harbour_scene_%28colorized%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Theodore_de_Bry_-_Harbour_scene_(colorized).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portuguese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carracks" title="Carracks">carracks</a> unload cargo in Lisbon. Original engraving by <a href="/wiki/Theodor_de_Bry" title="Theodor de Bry">Theodor de Bry</a>, 1593, coloured at a later date.</div></div></div>\n<p>After a series of prolonged contacts with Ethiopia, the Portuguese embassy made contact with the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Ethiopian (Abyssinian) Kingdom</a> led by Rodrigo de Lima in 1520.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abir86_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abir86-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> This coincided with the Portuguese search for Prester John, as they soon associated the kingdom as his land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The fear of Turkish advances within the Portuguese and Ethiopian sectors also played a role in their alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abir86_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Abir86-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a> defeated the Ethiopians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shimbra_Kure" title="Battle of Shimbra Kure">battle of Shimbra Kure</a> in 1529, and Islam spread further in the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Highlands" title="Ethiopian Highlands">region</a>. Portugal responded by aiding king <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelawdewos_of_Ethiopia" title="Gelawdewos of Ethiopia">Gelawdewos</a> with Portuguese soldiers and muskets. Though the Ottomans responded with support of soldiers and muskets to the Adal Sultanate, after the death of the Adali sultan <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Ibrahim_al-Ghazi" title="Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Ghazi">Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Ghazi</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wayna_Daga" title="Battle of Wayna Daga">battle of Wayna Daga</a> in 1543, the joint Adal-Ottoman force retreated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2013p121_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2013p121-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Portuguese also made direct contact with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongolose</a> vassal state <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Ndongo</a> and its ruler Ngola Kiljuane in 1520, after the latter requested missionaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancall2007p207_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mancall2007p207-98">[98]</a></sup> Kongolese king <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Kongo" title="Afonso I of Kongo">Afonso I</a> interfered with the process with denunciations, and later sent a Kongo mission to Ndongo after the latter had arrested the Portuguese mission that came.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancall2007p207_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mancall2007p207-98">[98]</a></sup> The growing official and unofficial slave trading with Ndongo strained relations between Kongo and the Portuguese, and even had Portuguese ambassadors from Sao Tome support Ndongo against the Kingdom of Kongo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thornton2000pp100-101_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thornton2000pp100-101-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeywoodThornton2007p83_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-HeywoodThornton2007p83-100">[100]</a></sup> However, when the <a href="/wiki/Jaga_(Kongo)" title="Jaga (Kongo)">Jaga</a> attacked and conquered regions of Kongo in 1568, Portuguese assisted Kongo in their defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2013p175_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2013p175-101">[101]</a></sup> In response, the Kongo allowed the colonization of Luanda Island; Luanda was established by <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Dias_de_Novais" title="Paulo Dias de Novais">Paulo Dias de Novais</a> in 1576 and soon became a slave port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stapleton2013p175_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stapleton2013p175-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> De Novais\' subsequent alliance with Ndongo angered Luso-Africans who resented the influence from the Crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeywoodThornton2007p86_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-HeywoodThornton2007p86-103">[103]</a></sup> In 1579, Ndongo ruler Ngola Kiluanje kia Ndamdi massacred Portuguese and Kongolese residents in the Ndongo capital <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Kabasa</a> under the influence of Portuguese renegades. Both the Portuguese and Kongo fought against Ndongo, and off-and-on warfare between the Ndongo and Portugal would persist for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancall2007pp208-211_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mancall2007pp208-211-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Missionary_expeditions">Missionary expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Missionary expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_(1635)_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1340" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png/220px-Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png/330px-Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png/440px-Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_%281635%29_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Francis_Xavier_taking_leave_of_King_John_III_(1635)_-_Jos%C3%A9_Avelar_Rebelo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Francis_Xavier" title="St. Francis Xavier">St. Francis Xavier</a> requesting <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III of Portugal</a> for a missionary expedition in Asia.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1542, Jesuit missionary <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a> arrived in Goa at the service of King <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III of Portugal</a>, in charge of an <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Nunciature" title="Apostolic Nunciature">Apostolic Nunciature</a>. At the same time Francisco Zeimoto, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Mota" title="Ant&#243;nio Mota">Ant&#243;nio Mota</a>, and other traders arrived in Japan for the first time. According to <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Mendes_Pinto" title="Fern&#227;o Mendes Pinto">Fern&#227;o Mendes Pinto</a>, who claimed to be in this journey, they arrived at <a href="/wiki/Tanegashima" title="Tanegashima">Tanegashima</a>, where the locals were impressed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanegashima_(Japanese_matchlock)" title="Tanegashima (Japanese matchlock)">firearms</a>, that would be immediately made by the Japanese on a large scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pacey1991_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pacey1991-105">[105]</a></sup> By 1570 the Portuguese bought part of a Japanese port where they founded a small part of the city of <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> and it became the major trading port in Japan in the triangular trade with China and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b195_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b195-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Portuguese were soundly defeated in their attempt to capture wealthy Somali <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">harbor</a> cities on the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Somali coast</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merca" title="Merca">Merca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barawa" title="Barawa">Barawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hobyo" title="Hobyo">Hobyo</a> by the powerful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_people" title="Somali people">Somalis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ajuran_Sultanate" title="Ajuran Sultanate">Ajuran Empire</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guarding its trade from both European and Asian competitors, Portugal dominated not only the trade between Asia and Europe, but also much of the trade between different regions of Asia and Africa, such as India, Indonesia, China, and Japan. <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> missionaries, followed the Portuguese to spread <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> to Asia and Africa with mixed success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto262-265_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto262-265-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization_efforts_in_the_Americas">Colonization efforts in the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Colonization efforts in the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese colonization of the Americas</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="583" data-file-width="946" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG/300px-Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG/450px-Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG/600px-Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reinel_Reinel_LopoHomem_1519.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Portuguese mapped and claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portugal_Cove-St._Philip%27s" title="Portugal Cove-St. Philip\'s">Canada</a> in 1499 and 1500s</div></div></div>\n<p>Based on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, the Portuguese Crown, under the kings Manuel I, John III and Sebastian, also claimed territorial rights in North America (reached by <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> in 1497 and 1498). To that end, in 1499 and 1500, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Fernandes_Lavrador" title="Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador">Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador</a> explored <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and the north Atlantic coast of Canada, which accounts for the appearance of "Labrador" on topographical maps of the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius464_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius464-112">[112]</a></sup> Subsequently, in 1500&#8211;1501 and 1502, the brothers <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">Gaspar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Corte-Real" title="Miguel Corte-Real">Miguel Corte-Real</a> explored what is today the Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, and Greenland, claiming these lands for Portugal. In 1506, King Manuel I created taxes for the cod fisheries in Newfoundland waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Around 1521, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_%C3%81lvares_Fagundes" title="Jo&#227;o &#193;lvares Fagundes">Jo&#227;o &#193;lvares Fagundes</a> was granted <a href="/wiki/Donat%C3%A1rio" title="Donat&#225;rio">donatary</a> rights to the inner islands of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_St._Lawrence" title="Gulf of St. Lawrence">Gulf of St. Lawrence</a> and also created a settlement on <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> to serve as a base for cod fishing. Pressure from natives and competing European fisheries prevented a permanent establishment and was abandoned five years later. Several attempts to establish settlements in Newfoundland over the next half-century also failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009a116_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009a116-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Within a few years after Cabral arrived from Brazil, competition came along from France. In 1503, an expedition under the command of <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Coelho" title="Gon&#231;alo Coelho">Gon&#231;alo Coelho</a> reported French raids on the Brazilian coasts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HerringHerring214_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-HerringHerring214-115">[115]</a></sup> and explorer <a href="/wiki/Binot_Paulmier_de_Gonneville" title="Binot Paulmier de Gonneville">Binot Paulmier de Gonneville</a> traded for brazilwood after making contact in southern Brazil a year later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Expeditions sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> along the North American coast directly violated of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesilhas" title="Treaty of Tordesilhas">Treaty of Tordesilhas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PickettPickett14_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-PickettPickett14-117">[117]</a></sup> By 1531, the French had stationed a trading post off of an island on the Brazilian coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PickettPickett14_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-PickettPickett14-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The increase in brazilwood smuggling from the French led <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_III" title="Jo&#227;o III">Jo&#227;o III</a> to press an effort to establish effective occupation of the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p76_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p76-118">[118]</a></sup> In 1531, a royal expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Martim_Afonso_de_Sousa" title="Martim Afonso de Sousa">Martim Afonso de Sousa</a> and his brother Pero Lopes went to patrol the whole Brazilian coast, banish the French, and create some of the first colonial towns &#8211; among them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Brazil" title="S&#227;o Vicente, Brazil">S&#227;o Vicente</a>, in 1532.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008pp76-78_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008pp76-78-119">[119]</a></sup> Sousa returned to Lisbon a year later to become <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">governor of India</a> and never returned to Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeOliveira254_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeOliveira254-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p78_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p78-121">[121]</a></sup> The French attacks did cease to an extent after retaliation led to the Portuguese paying the French to stop attacking Portuguese ships throughout the Atlantic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PickettPickett14_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-PickettPickett14-117">[117]</a></sup> but the attacks would continue to be a problem well into the 1560s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2005pp694-696_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2005pp694-696-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capitanias.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2031" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Capitanias.jpg/220px-Capitanias.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Capitanias.jpg/330px-Capitanias.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Capitanias.jpg/440px-Capitanias.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capitanias.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map from 1574 showing the 15 hereditary <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">captaincy colonies of Brazil</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Upon de Sousa\'s arrival and success, fifteen latitudinal tracts, theoretically to span from the coast to the Tordesillas limit, were decreed by Jo&#227;o III on 28 September 1532.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeOliveira254_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeOliveira254-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2005p694_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2005p694-123">[123]</a></sup> The plot of the lands formed as a hereditary <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil#Captaincies" title="Colonial Brazil">captaincies</a> (Capitanias Heredit&#225;rias) to grantees rich enough to support settlement, as had been done successfully in <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Cape_Verde" title="Colonial Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiffieWinius310_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiffieWinius310-124">[124]</a></sup> Each <a href="/wiki/Captain-major" title="Captain-major">captain-major</a> was to build settlements, grant allotments and administer justice, being responsible for developing and taking the costs of colonization, although not being the owner: he could transmit it to offspring, but not sell it. Twelve recipients came from Portuguese gentry who become prominent in Africa and India and senior officials of the court, such as <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_Barros" title="Jo&#227;o de Barros">Jo&#227;o de Barros</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deAbreu1998_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-deAbreu1998-125">[125]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the fifteen original captaincies, only two, <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">Pernambuco</a> and S&#227;o Vicente, prospered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeOliveira255-56_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeOliveira255-56-126">[126]</a></sup> Both were dedicated to the crop of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, and the settlers managed to maintain alliances with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_Peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous Peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a>. The rise of the sugar industry came about because the Crown took the easiest sources of profit (brazilwood, spices, etc.), leaving settlers to come up with new revenue sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeOliveira255_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeOliveira255-127">[127]</a></sup> The establishment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> industry demanded intensive labor that would be met with Native American and, later, African slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto111-119_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto111-119-128">[128]</a></sup> Deeming the <i>capitanias</i> system ineffective, Jo&#227;o III decided to centralize the government of the colony in order to "give help and assistance" to grantees. In 1548 he created the first General Government, sending in <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A9_de_Sousa" title="Tom&#233; de Sousa">Tom&#233; de Sousa</a> as first governor and selecting a capital at the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_All_Saints" title="Bay of All Saints">Bay of All Saints</a>, making it at the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_of_Bahia" title="Captaincy of Bahia">Captaincy of Bahia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lockhart190-191_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lockhart190-191-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bakewell496_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bakewell496-130">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tom&#233; de Sousa built the capital of Brazil, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvador,_Brazil" title="Salvador, Brazil">Salvador</a>, at the Bay of All Saints in 1549.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mahoney246_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mahoney246-131">[131]</a></sup> Among de Sousa\'s 1000 man expedition were soldiers, workers, and six <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_da_N%C3%B3brega" title="Manuel da N&#243;brega">Manuel da N&#243;brega</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russell-Wood1968p47_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Russell-Wood1968p47-132">[132]</a></sup> The Jesuits would have an essential role in the colonization of Brazil, including S&#227;o Vicente, and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="S&#227;o Paulo">S&#227;o Paulo</a>, the latter which N&#243;brega co-founded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ladle185_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ladle185-133">[133]</a></sup> Along with the Jesuit missions later came disease among the natives, among them <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Subsequently, the French would resettle in Portuguese territory at <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay" title="Guanabara Bay">Guanabara Bay</a>, which would be called <a href="/wiki/France_Antarctique" title="France Antarctique">France Antarctique</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p86_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p86-135">[135]</a></sup> While a Portuguese ambassador was sent to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> to report the French intrusion, Joao III appointed <a href="/wiki/Mem_de_S%C3%A1" title="Mem de S&#225;">Mem de S&#225;</a> as new Brazilian governor general, and S&#225; left for Brazil in 1557.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p86_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p86-135">[135]</a></sup> By 1560, S&#225; and his forces had expelled the combined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huguenot" title="Huguenot">Huguenot</a>, Scottish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calvinist" title="Calvinist">Calvinist</a>, and slave forces from France Antarctique, but left survivors after burning their fortifications and villages. These survivors would settle <a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%B3ria,_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Gl&#243;ria, Rio de Janeiro">Gloria Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flamengo,_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Flamengo, Rio de Janeiro">Flamengo Beach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Governador_Island" title="Governador Island">Parapapu&#227;</a> with the assistance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tup%C3%AD_people" title="Tup&#237; people">Tamoio</a> natives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p90_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p90-136">[136]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tamoio had been allied with the French since the settlement of France Antarctique, and despite the French loss in 1560, the Tamoio were still a threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Treece31_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Treece31-137">[137]</a></sup> They launched two attacks in 1561 and 1564 (the latter event was assisting the French), and were nearly successful with each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008pp91-92_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008pp91-92-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> By this time period, Manuel de N&#243;brega, along with fellow Jesuit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="Jos&#233; de Anchieta">Jos&#233; de Anchieta</a>, took part as members of attacks on the Tamoios and as spies for their resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Treece31_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Treece31-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008pp91-92_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008pp91-92-138">[138]</a></sup> From 1565 through 1567 Mem de S&#225; and his forces eventually destroyed France Antarctique at Guanabara Bay. He and his nephew, <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A1" title="Est&#225;cio de S&#225;">Est&#225;cio de S&#225;</a>, then established the city of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> in 1567, after Mem de S&#225; proclaimed the area "S&#227;o Sebasti&#227;o do Rio de Janeiro" in 1565.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marley2008p96_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marley2008p96-140">[140]</a></sup> By 1575, the Tamoios had been subdued and essentially were extinct,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Treece31_137-2"><a href="#cite_note-Treece31-137">[137]</a></sup> and by 1580 the government became more of a <i>ouvidor general</i> rather than the <i>ouvidores</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schwartz1973p41_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz1973p41-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Iberian_Union.2C_Protestant_rivalry.2C_and_colonial_stasis_.281580.E2.80.931663.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Iberian_Union,_Protestant_rivalry,_and_colonial_stasis_(1580&#8211;1663)">Iberian Union, Protestant rivalry, and colonial stasis (1580&#8211;1663)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Iberian Union, Protestant rivalry, and colonial stasis (1580&#8211;1663)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Portugal" title="Council of Portugal">Council of Portugal</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/300px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/450px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/600px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Luso-Hispanic (or Iberian) Empire</a> in 1598, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip I and II</a>, King of Portugal and Spain.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1580, King <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> invaded Portugal after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1580_Portuguese_succession_crisis" title="1580 Portuguese succession crisis">crisis of succession</a> brought about by King <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian of Portugal">Sebastian of Portugal</a>\'s death during a disastrous <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A1cer_Quibir" title="Battle of Alc&#225;cer Quibir">Portuguese attack on Alc&#225;cer Quibir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> in 1578. At the Cortes of Tomar in 1581, Philip was crowned Philip I of Portugal, uniting the two crowns and overseas empires under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Habsburgs" title="Spanish Habsburgs">Spanish Habsburg</a> rule in a <a href="/wiki/Dynastic_union" title="Dynastic union">dynastic</a> <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamen177_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kamen177-142">[142]</a></sup> At Tomar, Philip promised to keep the empires legally distinct, leaving the administration of the Portuguese Empire to Portuguese nationals, with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Viceroys_of_Portugal_during_the_Iberian_Union" title="List of Viceroys of Portugal during the Iberian Union">Viceroy of Portugal</a> in Lisbon seeing to his interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyajian11_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boyajian11-143">[143]</a></sup> Philip even had the capital moved to Lisbon for a two-year period (1581&#8211;83) due to it being the most important city in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher8_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher8-144">[144]</a></sup> All the Portuguese colonies accepted the new state of affairs except for the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, which held out for <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio,_Prior_of_Crato" title="Ant&#243;nio, Prior of Crato">Ant&#243;nio</a>, a Portuguese rival claimant to the throne who had garnered the support of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_de_Medici" title="Catherine de Medici">Catherine de Medici</a> of France in exchange for the promise to cede Brazil. Spanish forces eventually captured the islands in 1583.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson104-105_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson104-105-145">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tordesillas boundary between <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> and Portuguese control in South America was then increasingly ignored by the Portuguese, who pressed beyond it into the heart of Brazil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyajian11_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boyajian11-143">[143]</a></sup> allowing them to expand the territory to the west. Exploratory missions were carried out both ordered by the government, the "entradas" (entries), and by private initiative, the "bandeiras" (flags), by the "<a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">bandeirantes</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer386_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer386-146">[146]</a></sup> These expeditions lasted for years venturing into unmapped regions, initially to capture natives and force them into slavery, and later focusing on finding gold, silver and diamond mines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto111,117_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto111,117-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa,_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2362" data-file-width="2909" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg/220px-La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg/330px-La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg/440px-La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa%2C_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_recuperaci%C3%B3n_de_Bah%C3%ADa,_Ma%C3%ADno.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Recovery_of_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Todos_los_Santos" title="The Recovery of Bah&#237;a de Todos los Santos">The Recovery of S&#227;o Salvador da Bahia de Todos os Santos</a>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_III_of_Portugal" title="Philip III of Portugal">Philip III of Portugal</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>However, the union meant that Spain dragged Portugal into its conflicts with England, France and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, countries which were beginning to establish their own overseas empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson105_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson105-148">[148]</a></sup> The primary threat came from the Dutch, who had been engaged in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eighty_Years_War" title="Eighty Years War">struggle for independence</a> against Spain since 1568. In 1581, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Seven Provinces</a> gained independence from the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg rule</a>, leading Philip II to prohibit commerce with Dutch ships, including in Brazil where <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> had invested large sums in financing sugar production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas159_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas159-149">[149]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Spanish imperial trade networks now were opened to Portuguese merchants, which was particularly lucrative for Portuguese slave traders who could now sell slaves in Spanish America at a higher price than could be fetched in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lockhart250_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lockhart250-150">[150]</a></sup> In addition to this newly acquired access to the Spanish <i><a href="/wiki/Asiento" title="Asiento">asientos</a></i>, the Portuguese were able to solve their bullion shortage issues with access to the production of the silver mining in Peru and Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt163_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt163-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> was also incorporated into the Macau-Nagasaki trading network, allowing Macanese of Portuguese descent to act as trading agents for Philippine Spaniards and use Spanish silver from the Americas in trade with China, and they later drew competition with the Dutch East India Company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b186_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b186-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1592, during the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585%E2%80%931604)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585&#8211;1604)">war with Spain</a>, an English fleet captured a large Portuguese carrack off the Azores, the <a href="/wiki/Madre_de_Deus" title="Madre de Deus">Madre de Deus</a>, which was loaded with 900 tons of merchandise from India and China estimated at half a million <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pounds</a> (nearly half the size of English Treasury at the time).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> This foretaste of the riches of the East galvanized English interest in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> That same year, <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_de_Houtman" title="Cornelis de Houtman">Cornelis de Houtman</a> was sent by Dutch merchants to Lisbon, to gather as much information as he could about the Spice Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b186_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b186-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lach200_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lach200-155">[155]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dutch eventually realized the importance of Goa in breaking up the Portuguese empire in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. In 1583, merchant and explorer <a href="/wiki/Jan_Huyghen_van_Linschoten" title="Jan Huyghen van Linschoten">Jan Huyghen van Linschoten</a> (1563 &#8211; 8 February 1611), formerly the Dutch secretary of the Archbishop of Goa, had acquired information while serving in that position that contained the location of secret Portuguese trade routes throughout Asia, including those to the East Indies and Japan. It was published in 1595; the text was then included in the larger volume published in 1596 under the title "Itinerario: voyage, ofte schipvaert van Jan Huygen van Linschoten naer Oost ofte Portugaels Indien, 1579&#8211;1592". Dutch and English interests used this new information, leading to their commercial expansion, including the foundation of the English <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> in 1600, and the Dutch East India Company in 1602. These developments allowed the entry of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chartered_companies" title="Chartered companies">chartered companies</a> into the East Indies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crow1992_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crow1992-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowenLincoln2002_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-BowenLincoln2002-157">[157]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meirelles-guararapes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="962" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Meirelles-guararapes.jpg/220px-Meirelles-guararapes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Meirelles-guararapes.jpg/330px-Meirelles-guararapes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Meirelles-guararapes.jpg/440px-Meirelles-guararapes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meirelles-guararapes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Portuguese victory at the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Guararapes" title="Second Battle of Guararapes">Second Battle of Guararapes</a> ended Dutch presence in <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">Pernambuco</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dutch took their fight overseas, attacking <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> and Portuguese colonies and beginning the <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" title="Dutch&#8211;Portuguese War">Dutch&#8211;Portuguese War</a>, which would last for over sixty years (1602&#8211;1663). Other <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> nations, such as Protestant England, assisted the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a> in the war. The Dutch attained victories in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> with assistance of various indigenous allies, eventually wrenching control of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Malacca" title="Portuguese Malacca">Malacca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Ceylon" title="Portuguese Ceylon">Ceylon</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_da_Mina" title="S&#227;o Jorge da Mina">S&#227;o Jorge da Mina</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> also had regional control of the lucrative sugar-producing region of northeast <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Brazil</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Luanda</a>, but the Portuguese regained these territories after considerable struggle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b73-74,168-171,226-231_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b73-74,168-171,226-231-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Meanwhile, in the Arabian Peninsula, the Portuguese also lost control of <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Ormuz_(1622)" title="Capture of Ormuz (1622)">Ormuz</a> by a joint alliance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavid_Empire" title="Safavid Empire">Safavids</a> and the English in 1622, and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Yaruba_dynasty" title="Yaruba dynasty">Al-Ya\'arubs</a> would capture <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a> in 1650.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b169_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b169-160">[160]</a></sup> They would continue to use Muscat as a base for repetitive incursions within the Indian Ocean, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Jesus" title="Siege of Fort Jesus">including capturing Fort Jesus in 1698</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b350_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b350-161">[161]</a></sup> In Ethiopia and Japan in the 1630s, the ousting of missionaries by local leaders severed influence in the respective regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Second_era_.281663.E2.80.931825.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_era_(1663&#8211;1825)">Second era (1663&#8211;1825)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Second era (1663&#8211;1825)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1640%E2%80%931777)" title="History of Portugal (1640&#8211;1777)">History of Portugal (1640&#8211;1777)</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1777%E2%80%931834)" title="History of Portugal (1777&#8211;1834)">History of Portugal (1777&#8211;1834)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Portugal_(1667).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="957" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Portugal_%281667%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Portugal_(1667).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of Portugal (1667&#8211;1706). From the 15th&#8211;19th centuries the Portuguese flags all looked similar to this.</div></div></div>\n<p>The loss of colonies was one of the reasons that contributed to the end of the personal union with Spain. In 1640 John IV was proclaimed King of Portugal and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a> began. Even before the war\'s final resolution, the crown established the Overseas Council, conceived in 1642 on the short-lived model of the Council of India (1604&#8211;1614), and established in 1643, it was the governing body for most of the Portuguese overseas empire. The exceptions were North Africa, Madeira, and the Azores. All correspondence concerning overseas possessions were funneled through the council. When the Portuguese court fled to Brazil in 1807, following the Napoleonic invasion of Iberia, Brazil was removed from the jurisdiction of the council. It made recommendations concerning personnel for the administrative, fiscal, and military, as well as bishops of overseas dioceses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> A distinguished seventeenth-century member was <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_S%C3%A1" title="Salvador de S&#225;">Salvador de S&#225;</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Portuguese_India.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1404" data-file-width="1709" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Map_of_Portuguese_India.png/220px-Map_of_Portuguese_India.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Map_of_Portuguese_India.png/330px-Map_of_Portuguese_India.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Map_of_Portuguese_India.png/440px-Map_of_Portuguese_India.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Portuguese_India.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a> (1502&#8211;1961)</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1661 the Portuguese offered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bombay" title="Bombay">Bombay</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Tangier" title="Portuguese Tangier">Tangier</a> to England as part of a <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a>, and over the next hundred years the English gradually became the dominant trader in India, gradually excluding the trade of other powers. In 1668 Spain recognized the end of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> and in exchange Portugal ceded <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> to the Spanish crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cowans2003_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cowans2003-166">[166]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Portuguese were defeated by the Indian rulers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimnaji_Appa" title="Chimnaji Appa">Chimnaji Appa</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Maratha Empire</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahmed330_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmed330-168">[168]</a></sup> and by <a href="/wiki/Shivappa_Nayaka" title="Shivappa Nayaka">Shivappa Nayaka</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keladi_Nayaka_Kingdom" title="Keladi Nayaka Kingdom">Keladi Nayaka Kingdom</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> and at the end of confrontations with the Dutch, Portugal was only able to cling onto <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> and several minor bases in India, and managed to regain territories in <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Brazil</a> and Africa, but lost forever to prominence in Asia as trade was diverted through increasing numbers of English, Dutch and French trading posts. Thus, throughout the century, Brazil gained increasing importance to the empire, which exported <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilwood" title="Brazilwood">Brazilwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BethencourtCurto111,117_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-BethencourtCurto111,117-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minas_Gerais_and_the_gold_industry">Minas Gerais and the gold industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Minas Gerais and the gold industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1693, gold was discovered at <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> in Brazil. Major discoveries of gold and, later, diamonds in Minas Gerais, <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a> and Goi&#225;s led to a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazil_Gold_Rush" title="Brazil Gold Rush">gold rush</a>", with a large influx of migrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxer168_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer168-170">[170]</a></sup> The village became the new economic center of the empire, with rapid settlement and some conflicts. This gold cycle led to the creation of an internal market and attracted a large number of immigrants. By 1739, at the apex of the mining boom, the population of Minas Gerais was somewhere between 200,000 and 250,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b268-69_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b268-69-171">[171]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1851" data-file-width="1436" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg/170px-Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg/255px-Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg/340px-Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Cortes_1822.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Portuguese Cortes</a> sought the disbandment of the United Kingdom.</div></div></div>\n<p>The gold rush considerably increased the revenue of the Portuguese crown, who charged a fifth of all the ore mined, or the "fifth". Diversion and smuggling were frequent, along with altercations between <i>Paulistas</i> (residents of S&#227;o Paulo) and <i>Emboabas</i> (immigrants from Portugal and other regions in Brazil), so a whole set of bureaucratic controls began in 1710 with the captaincy of S&#227;o Paulo and Minas Gerais. By 1718, S&#227;o Paulo and Minas Gerais became two captaincies, with eight <i>vilas</i> created in the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bethell203_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell203-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b267-68_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b267-68-173">[173]</a></sup> The crown also restricted the diamond mining within its jurisdiction and to private contractors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b267-68_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b267-68-173">[173]</a></sup> In spite of gold galvanizing global trade, the plantation industry became the leading export for Brazil during this period; sugar constituted at 50% of the exports (with gold at 46%) in 1760.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b268-69_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b268-69-171">[171]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Africans and Afro-Brazilians became the largest group of people in Minas Gerais. Slaves labeled as \'Minas\' and \'Angolas\' rose in high demand during the boom. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Akan_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Akan peoples (page does not exist)">Akan</a> within the \'Minas\' group had a reputation to have been experts in extrapolating gold in their native regions, and became the preferred group. In spite of the high death rate associated with the slaves involved in the mining industry, the owners that allowed slaves that extracted above the minimum amount of gold to keep the excesses, which in turn led to the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Manumission" title="Manumission">manumission</a>. Those that became free partook in artisan jobs such as cobblers, tailors, and blacksmiths. In spite of free blacks and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mulattoes" title="Mulattoes">mulattoes</a> playing a large role in Minas Gerais, the number of them that received marginalization was greater there than in any other region in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b273-275_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b273-275-174">[174]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gold discovered in Mato Grosso and Goi&#225;s sparked an interest to solidify the western borders of the colony. In the 1730s contact with Spanish outposts occurred more frequently, and the Spanish threatened to launch a military expedition in order to remove them. This failed to happen and by the 1750s the Portuguese were able to implant a political stronghold in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b288_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b288-175">[175]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1755 Lisbon suffered a catastrophic <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">earthquake</a>, which together with a subsequent <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> killed between 40,000&#8211;60,000 people out of a population of 275,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KozakCermak131_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-KozakCermak131-176">[176]</a></sup> This sharply checked Portuguese colonial ambitions in the late 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramasamy2006_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramasamy2006-177">[177]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to economic historians, Portugal\'s colonial trade had a substantial positive impact on Portuguese economic growth, 1500&#8211;1800. Leonor Costa et al. conclude:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>intercontinental trade had a substantial and increasingly positive impact on economic growth. In the heyday of colonial expansion, eliminating the economic links to empire would have reduced Portugal&#8217;s per capita income by roughly a fifth. While the empire helped the domestic economy it was not sufficient to annul the tendency towards decline in relation to Europe&#8217;s advanced core which set in from the 17th century onwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pombaline_and_post-Pombaline_Brazil">Pombaline and post-Pombaline Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pombaline and post-Pombaline Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazil_(1817).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1985" data-file-width="2008" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Brazil_%281817%29.svg/280px-Brazil_%281817%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Brazil_%281817%29.svg/420px-Brazil_%281817%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Brazil_%281817%29.svg/560px-Brazil_%281817%29.svg.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazil_(1817).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Provinces of the Portuguese Empire in the Americas by 1817.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2655" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/220px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/330px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg/440px-Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Imperios_Espa%C3%B1ol_y_Portugu%C3%A9s_1790.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish and Portuguese empires in 1790.</div></div></div>\n<p>Unlike Spain, Portugal did not divide its <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">colonial territory in America</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitania" title="Capitania">captaincies</a> created there functioned under a centralized administration in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvador_da_Bahia" title="Salvador da Bahia">Salvador</a>, which reported directly to the Crown in Lisbon. The 18th century was marked by increasing centralization of royal power throughout the Portuguese empire. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a>, who protected the natives against slavery, were brutally suppressed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Marquis of Pombal">Marquis of Pombal</a>, which led to the dissolution of the order in the region by 1759.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009a298-302_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009a298-302-179">[179]</a></sup> Pombal wished to improve the status of the natives by declaring them free and increasing the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> population by encouraging intermarriage between them and the white population. Indigenous freedom decreased in contrast to its period under the Jesuits, and the response to intermarriage was lukewarm at best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b288-89_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b288-89-180">[180]</a></sup> The crown\'s revenue from gold declined and plantation revenue increased by the time of Pombal, and he made provisions to improve each. Although he failed to spike the gold revenue, two short-term companies he established for the plantation economy drove a significant increase in production of cotton, rice, cacao, tobacco, sugar. Slave labor increased as well as involvement from the textile economy. The economic development as a whole was inspired by elements of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> in mainland Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b277-79,_283-84_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b277-79,_283-84-181">[181]</a></sup> However, the diminished influence from states such as the United Kingdom increased the Kingdom\'s dependence upon Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Encouraged by the example of the United States of America, which had won its independence from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a>, the colonial province of <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> attempted to achieve the same objective in 1789. However, the <a href="/wiki/Inconfid%C3%AAncia_Mineira" title="Inconfid&#234;ncia Mineira">Inconfid&#234;ncia Mineira</a> failed, its leaders were arrested, and of the participants in the insurrections, the one of lowest social position, <a href="/wiki/Tiradentes" title="Tiradentes">Tiradentes</a>, was hanged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bethell163-164_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell163-164-183">[183]</a></sup> Among the conspiracies led by the Afro- population was the Bahian revolt in 1798, led primarily by Jo&#227;o de Deus do Nascimento. Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, leaders proposed a society without slavery, food prices would be lowered, and trade restriction abolished. Impoverished social conditions and a high cost of living were among reasons of the revolt. Authorities diffused the plot before major action began; they executed four of the conspirators and exiled several others were exiled to the Atlantic Coast of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b296-297_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b296-297-184">[184]</a></sup> Several more smaller-scale slave rebellions and revolts would occur from 1801 and 1816 and fears within Brazil were that these events would lead to a <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">"second Haiti"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In spite of the conspiracies, the rule of Portugal in Brazil was not under serious threat. Historian A.R. Disney states that the colonists did not until the transferring of the Kingdom in 1808 assert influence of policy changing due to direct contact,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney2009b298_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney2009b298-186">[186]</a></sup> and historian Gabriel Paquette mentions that the threats in Brazil were largely unrealized in Portugal until 1808 because of effective policing and espionage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> More revolts would occur after the arrival of the court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazilian_Independence">Brazilian Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Brazilian Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil</a>; <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil</a>; and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1268" data-file-width="2271" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/220px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/330px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/440px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Independence" title="Brazilian Independence">Brazilian Independence</a> crippled the Portuguese Empire, both economically and politically, for a long time.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1808, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> invaded Portugal, and <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">Dom Jo&#227;o</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" title="Prince Regent">Prince Regent</a> in place of his mother, <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">Dona Maria I</a>, ordered the transfer of the royal court to Brazil. In 1815 Brazil was elevated to the status of Kingdom, the Portuguese state officially becoming the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a> (<i>Reino Unido de Portugal, Brasil e Algarves</i>), and the capital was transferred from Lisbon to Rio de Janeiro, the only instance of a European country being ruled from one of its colonies. There was also the election of Brazilian representatives to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Cortes Constitucionais Portuguesas</a> (Portuguese Constitutional Courts), the Parliament that assembled in Lisbon in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1820" title="Liberal Revolution of 1820">Liberal Revolution of 1820</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bethell177-178_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell177-178-189">[189]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the royal family returned to Portugal in 1821, the interlude led to a growing desire for independence amongst Brazilians. In 1822, the son of Dom Jo&#227;o VI, then prince-regent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dom_Pedro_I" title="Dom Pedro I">Dom Pedro I</a>, proclaimed the independence of Brazil on September 7, 1822, and was crowned Emperor of the new <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>. Unlike the Spanish colonies of South America, Brazil\'s independence was achieved without significant bloodshed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Angus1837_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Angus1837-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levine2003_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levine2003-191">[191]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Third_era_.281822.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_era_(1822&#8211;1999)">Third era (1822&#8211;1999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Third era (1822&#8211;1999)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_East_Africa" title="Portuguese East Africa">Portuguese East Africa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa">Portuguese West Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">Liberal Wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1834%E2%80%931910)" title="History of Portugal (1834&#8211;1910)">History of Portugal (1834&#8211;1910)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jesuit_Convent,_Macao.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1082" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg/220px-Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg/330px-Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg/440px-Jesuit_Convent%2C_Macao.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jesuit_Convent,_Macao.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fa&#231;ade of <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_College,_Macau" title="St. Paul\'s College, Macau">St. Paul\'s College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, 1854</div></div></div>\n<p>At the height of <a href="/wiki/European_colonialism" title="European colonialism">European colonialism</a> in the 19th century, Portugal had lost its territory in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and all but a few bases in Asia. During this phase, Portuguese colonialism focused on expanding its outposts in Africa into nation-sized territories to compete with other European powers there. Portugal pressed into the hinterland of Angola and Mozambique, and explorers <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_de_Serpa_Pinto" title="Alexandre de Serpa Pinto">Serpa Pinto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermenegildo_Capelo" title="Hermenegildo Capelo">Hermenegildo Capelo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Ivens" title="Roberto Ivens">Roberto Ivens</a> were among the first Europeans to cross Africa west to east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitt1995pp335-336_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitt1995pp335-336-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corrado18_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado18-193">[193]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="British_Ultimatum_and_end_of_Portuguese_monarchy_.281890.E2.80.931910.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Ultimatum_and_end_of_Portuguese_monarchy_(1890&#8211;1910)">British Ultimatum and end of Portuguese monarchy (1890&#8211;1910)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: British Ultimatum and end of Portuguese monarchy (1890&#8211;1910)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chaimite.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Chaimite.jpg/220px-Chaimite.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Chaimite.jpg/330px-Chaimite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/Chaimite.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chaimite.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the 19th century, Portugal launched campaigns to solidify Portuguese Africa.</div></div></div>\n<p>The project to connect the two colonies, the <a href="/wiki/Pink_Map" title="Pink Map">Pink Map</a>, was the main objective of Portuguese policy in the 1880s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisboa134_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lisboa134-194">[194]</a></sup> However, the idea was unacceptable to the British, who had their own aspirations of contiguous British territory running from <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Ultimatum" title="British Ultimatum">British Ultimatum</a> of 1890 was imposed upon King <a href="/wiki/Carlos_I_of_Portugal" title="Carlos I of Portugal">Carlos I of Portugal</a> and the Pink Map came to an end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisboa134_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lisboa134-194">[194]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The King\'s reaction to the ultimatum was exploited by republicans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisboa134_194-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lisboa134-194">[194]</a></sup> In 1908 King Carlos and Prince <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Filipe,_Prince_Royal_of_Portugal" title="Lu&#237;s Filipe, Prince Royal of Portugal">Lu&#237;s Filipe</a> were murdered in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>. Lu&#237;s Filipe\'s brother, Manuel, became King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">Manuel II of Portugal</a>. Two years later he was overthrown and Portugal became a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wheeler48-61_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wheeler48-61-195">[195]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_campaign_in_Angola" title="German campaign in Angola">German campaign in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_I)" title="East African Campaign (World War I)">East African Campaign (World War I)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portugal_during_World_War_I" title="Portugal during World War I">Portugal during World War I</a></div>\n<p>In 1914, the German Empire formulated plans to usurp Angola from Portuguese control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vincent-Smith1974_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent-Smith1974-196">[196]</a></sup> Skirmishes between Portuguese and German soldiers ensued, resulting in reinforcements being sent from the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The main objective of these soldiers was to recapture the <a href="/wiki/Kionga_Triangle" title="Kionga Triangle">Kionga Triangle</a>, in northern Mozambique, the territory having been subjugated by Germany.\nIn 1916, after Portugal interned German ships in Lisbon, Germany declared war on Portugal. Portugal followed suit, thus entering World War I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wheeler128_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wheeler128-198">[198]</a></sup>\nEarly in the war, Portugal was involved mainly in supplying the Allies positioned in France. In 1916, there was only one attack on the Portuguese territory, in <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> In 1917, one of the actions taken by Portugal was to assist Britain in its timber industry, imperative to the war effort. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forestry_Corps" title="Canadian Forestry Corps">Canadian Forestry Corps</a>, Portuguese personnel established logging infrastructure in an area now referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Fireplace" title="Portuguese Fireplace">Portuguese Fireplace</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout 1917 Portugal dispatched contingents of troops to the Allied front in France. Midway in the year, Portugal suffered its first World War I casualty. In Portuguese Africa, Portugal and the British fought numerous battles against the Germans in both Mozambique and Angola. Later in the year, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-boats" title="U-boats">U-boats</a> entered Portuguese waters again and once more attacked Madeira, sinking multiple Portuguese ships. Through the beginning of 1918, Portugal continued to fight along the Allied front against Germany, including participation in the infamous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Lys" title="Battle of La Lys">Battle of La Lys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> As autumn approached, Germany found success in both Portuguese Africa and against Portuguese vessels, sinking multiple ships. After nearly three years of fighting (from a Portuguese perspective), World War I ended, with an armistice being signed by Germany. At the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Versailles Conference</a>, Portugal regained control of all its lost territory, but did not retain possession (by the principle of <a href="/wiki/Uti_possidetis" title="Uti possidetis">uti possidetis</a>) of territories gained during the war, except for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kionga" title="Kionga">Kionga</a>, a port city in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portuguese territories in Africa eventually included the modern nations of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe">S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koffi2012_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koffi2012-203">[203]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Turmoil_and_decolonization_.281951.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Turmoil_and_decolonization_(1951&#8211;1999)">Turmoil and decolonization (1951&#8211;1999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Turmoil and decolonization (1951&#8211;1999)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Macau" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Macau">Transfer of sovereignty over Macau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Goa" title="Annexation of Goa">Annexation of Goa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png/280px-Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png/420px-Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png/560px-Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a
