class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Empire_20th_century.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the 20th century, Portugal no longer called itself an empire, but a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pluricontinental" title="Pluricontinental">pluricontinental</a> nation with overseas provinces.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the wake of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, decolonization movements began to gain momentum in the empires of the European powers. The ensuing <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> also created instabilities among Portuguese overseas populations, as the United States and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> vied to increase their spheres of influence. Following the granting of independence to India by <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> in 1947, and the decision by France to allow its <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">enclaves in India</a> to be incorporated into the newly independent nation, pressure was placed on Portugal to do the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> This was resisted by <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant&#243;nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant&#243;nio de Oliveira Salazar</a>, who had taken power in 1933. Salazar rebuffed a request in 1950 by <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Indian Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> to return the enclaves, viewing them as integral parts of Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The following year, the Portuguese constitution was amended to change the status of the colonies to overseas provinces. In 1954, a local uprising resulted in the overthrow of the Portuguese authorities in the Indian enclave of <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>. The existence of the remaining Portuguese colonies in India became increasingly untenable and Nehru enjoyed the support of almost all the Indian domestic political parties as well as the Soviet Union and its allies. In 1961, shortly after an uprising against the Portuguese in Angola, Nehru ordered the Indian Army into <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a>, which were quickly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1961_Indian_Annexation_of_Goa" title="1961 Indian Annexation of Goa">captured</a> and formally annexed the following year. Salazar refused to recognize the transfer of sovereignty, believing the territories to be merely occupied. The Province of Goa continued to be represented in the Portuguese National Assembly until 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson153_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson153-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1195" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/170px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/255px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/340px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant&#243;nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant&#243;nio de Oliveira Salazar</a> sought the preservation of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pluricontinental" title="Pluricontinental">pluricontinental</a> Portugal.</div></div></div>\n<p>The outbreak of violence in February 1961 in Angola was the beginning of the end of Portugal\'s empire in Africa. Portuguese army officers in Angola held the view that it would be incapable of dealing militarily with an outbreak of guerilla warfare and therefore that negotiations should begin with the independence movements. However, Salazar publicly stated his determination to keep the empire intact, and by the end of the year, 50,000 troops had been stationed there. The same year, the tiny Portuguese fort of S&#227;o Jo&#227;o Baptista de Ajud&#225; in <a href="/wiki/Ouidah" title="Ouidah">Ouidah</a>, a remnant of the West African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>, was annexed by the new government of Dahomey (now <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>) that had gained its independence from France. Unrest spread from Angola to Guinea, which rebelled in 1963, and Mozambique in 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson153_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson153-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rise of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> influence among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movimento_das_For%C3%A7as_Armadas" title="Movimento das For&#231;as Armadas">Movimento das For&#231;as Armadas</a>\'s military (MFA) and working class, and the cost and unpopularity of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> (1961&#8211;1974), in which Portugal resisted to the emerging nationalist guerrilla movements in some of its African territories, eventually led to the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> regime in 1974. Known as the "<a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>", one of the first acts of the MFA-led government which then came into power &#8211; the <a href="/wiki/National_Salvation_Junta" title="National Salvation Junta">National Salvation Junta</a> (<i>Junta de Salva&#231;&#227;o Nacional</i>) &#8211; was to end the wars and negotiate Portuguese withdrawal from its African colonies. These events prompted a mass exodus of Portuguese citizens from Portugal\'s African territories (mostly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Angola" title="Overseas Province of Angola">Angola</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Mozambique" title="Overseas Province of Mozambique">Mozambique</a>), creating over a million Portuguese refugees &#8211; the <i>retornados.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Portugal\'s new ruling authorities also recognized Goa and other Portuguese India\'s territories <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Goa" title="Invasion of Goa">invaded by India\'s military forces</a>, as Indian territories. Benin\'s claims over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jo%C3%A3o_Baptista_de_Ajud%C3%A1" title="S&#227;o Jo&#227;o Baptista de Ajud&#225;">S&#227;o Jo&#227;o Baptista de Ajud&#225;</a> were accepted by Portugal in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to one historian, Portuguese rulers were unwilling to meet the demands of their colonial subjects (unlike other European powers) in part because Portuguese elites believed that "Portugal lacked the means to conduct a successful &#8220;exit strategy&#8221; (akin to the &#8220;neocolonial&#8221; approach followed by the British, the French, or the Belgians)" and in part due to the lack of "a free and open debate [in Salazar\'s dictatorial state] on the costs of upholding an empire against the anti-colonial consensus that had prevailed in the United Nations since the early 1960s".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Civil wars in <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozambican_Civil_War" title="Mozambican Civil War">Mozambique</a> promptly broke out, with incoming communist governments formed by the former rebels (and backed by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Cuba, and other communist countries) fighting against insurgent groups supported by nations like <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>, South Africa, and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArnoldWiener11-12_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-ArnoldWiener11-12-210">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> also declared independence in 1975 by making an exodus of many Portuguese refugees to Portugal, which was also known as <i>retornados</i>. However, East Timor was almost immediately <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">invaded by neighbouring Indonesia</a>, which would later <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">occupied</a> it up until 1999. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Timor_Special_Autonomy_Referendum" title="East Timor Special Autonomy Referendum">United Nations-sponsored referendum</a> resulted in a majority of East Timorese choosing independence, which was finally achieved in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1987, Portugal signed the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Declaration_on_the_Question_of_Macau" title="Joint Declaration on the Question of Macau">Sino-Portuguese Joint Declaration</a> with the People\'s Republic of China to establish the process and conditions for the transfer of sovereignty of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Macau</a>, its last remaining colony. While this process was similar to <a href="/wiki/Sino-British_Joint_Declaration" title="Sino-British Joint Declaration">the agreement between the United Kingdom and China</a> two years earlier regarding <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, the Portuguese transfer to China was met with less resistance than that of Britain regarding Hong Kong, as Portugal had already recognized Macau as Chinese territory under Portuguese administration in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Under the transfer agreement, Macau is to be governed under a <a href="/wiki/One_country,_two_systems" title="One country, two systems">one country, two systems</a> policy, in which it will retain a high degree of autonomy and maintain its capitalist way of life for at least 50 years after the handover in 2049. The handover in 1999 officially marked the end of the Portuguese Empire and end of colonialism in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png/240px-Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png/360px-Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png/480px-Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Imp%C3%A9rio_total.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><span style="background-color:red; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Actual possessions<br/><span style="background-color:Olive; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Explorations<br/><span style="background-color:Orange; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Areas of influence and trade<br/><span style="background-color:Pink; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Claims of sovereignty<br/><span style="background-color:Green; color:white; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Trading posts<br/><span style="background-color:SkyBlue; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Main sea explorations, routes and areas of influence</div></div></div>\n<p>Presently, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP) serves as the cultural and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental</a> successor of the Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_NewsID46_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP_NewsID46-214">[214]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Macau was returned to China on 20 December 1999, under the terms of an agreement negotiated between People\'s Republic of China and Portugal twelve years earlier. Nevertheless, the Portuguese language remains co-official with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cantonese_Chinese" title="Cantonese Chinese">Cantonese Chinese</a> in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg/220px-S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg/330px-S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg/440px-S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A9_de_Santa_Catarina.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Se_Cathedral" title="Se Cathedral">Se Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, India, an example of Portuguese architecture and one of the largest churches in Asia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Currently, the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a> are the only overseas territories that remain politically linked to Portugal. Although Portugal began the process of decolonizing <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">East Timor</a> in 1975, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Macau</a> during 1999&#8211;2002 was sometimes considered Portugal\'s last remaining colony, as the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">Indonesian invasion of East Timor</a> was not justified by Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eight of the former colonies of Portugal have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographic_distribution_of_Portuguese" title="Geographic distribution of Portuguese">Portuguese as their official language</a>. Together with Portugal, they are now members of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, which when combined total 10,742,000&#160;km&#178;, or 7.2% of the Earth\'s landmass (148 939 063&#160;km&#178;).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> There are six associate observers of the CPLP: <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkey_(country)" title="Turkey (country)">Turkey</a>. Moreover, twelve candidate countries or regions have applied for membership to the CPLP and are awaiting approval.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_street_sign.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/220px-Macau_street_sign.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/330px-Macau_street_sign.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/440px-Macau_street_sign.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_street_sign.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> remains an official language in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> after the handover to China</div></div></div>\n<p>Today, Portuguese is one of the world\'s major languages, ranked sixth overall with approximately 240 million speakers around the globe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l&#237;ngua_portuguesa_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-l&#237;ngua_portuguesa-219">[219]</a></sup> It is the third most spoken language in the Americas, mainly due to Brazil, although there are also significant communities of lusophones in nations such as Canada, the US and Venezuela. In addition, there are numerous <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">Portuguese-based creole languages</a>, including the one utilized by the <a href="/wiki/Kristang_people" title="Kristang people">Kristang</a> people in <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>\n</p><p>For instance, as Portuguese merchants were presumably the first to introduce the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_orange" title="Sweet orange">sweet orange</a> in Europe, in several modern <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> the fruit has been named after them. Some examples are Albanian <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portokall#Albanian" title="wikt:portokall">portokall</a>, Bulgarian <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BB#Bulgarian" title="wikt:&#1087;&#1086;&#1088;&#1090;&#1086;&#1082;&#1072;&#1083;">&#1087;&#1086;&#1088;&#1090;&#1086;&#1082;&#1072;&#1083;</a> (<i>portokal</i>), Greek <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%81%CF%84%CE%BF%CE%BA%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B9#Greek" title="wikt:&#960;&#959;&#961;&#964;&#959;&#954;&#940;&#955;&#953;">&#960;&#959;&#961;&#964;&#959;&#954;&#940;&#955;&#953;</a> (<i>portokali</i>), Macedonian <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BB#Macedonian" title="wikt:&#1087;&#1086;&#1088;&#1090;&#1086;&#1082;&#1072;&#1083;">&#1087;&#1086;&#1088;&#1090;&#1086;&#1082;&#1072;&#1083;</a> (<i>portokal</i>), Persian <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%BE%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Persian" title="wikt:&#1662;&#1585;&#1578;&#1602;&#1575;&#1604;">&#1662;&#1585;&#1578;&#1602;&#1575;&#1604;</a> (<i>porteghal</i>), and Romanian <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portocal%C4%83#Romanian" title="wikt:portocal&#259;">portocal&#259;</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-plantname-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OstergrenBosse2011_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-OstergrenBosse2011-222">[222]</a></sup> Related names can be found in other languages, such as Arabic <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A8%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Arabic" title="wikt:&#1575;&#1604;&#1576;&#1585;&#1578;&#1602;&#1575;&#1604;">&#1575;&#1604;&#1576;&#1585;&#1578;&#1602;&#1575;&#1604;</a> (<i>bourtouqal</i>), <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%83%A4%E1%83%9D%E1%83%A0%E1%83%97%E1%83%9D%E1%83%AE%E1%83%90%E1%83%9A%E1%83%98#Georgian" title="wikt:&#4324;&#4317;&#4320;&#4311;&#4317;&#4334;&#4304;&#4314;&#4312;">&#4324;&#4317;&#4320;&#4311;&#4317;&#4334;&#4304;&#4314;&#4312;</a> (<i>p\'ort\'oxali</i>), Turkish <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portakal#Turkish" title="wikt:portakal">portakal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amharic" title="Amharic">Amharic</a> <i>birtukan</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-plantname-221">[221]</a></sup> Also, in <a href="/wiki/Regional_Italian" title="Regional Italian">southern Italian dialects</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">Neapolitan</a>), an orange is <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portogallo" title="wikt:portogallo">portogallo</a></i> or <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/it:purtuallo" title="wikt:it:purtuallo">purtuallo</a></i>, literally "(the) Portuguese (one)", in contrast to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Italian" title="Standard Italian">standard Italian</a> <i>arancia</i>.\n</p><p>In light of its international importance, Portugal and Brazil are leading a movement to include Portuguese as one of the <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_the_United_Nations" title="Official languages of the United Nations">official languages of the United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Portuguese_Empire" title="Evolution of the Portuguese Empire">Evolution of the Portuguese Empire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_inventions" title="Portuguese inventions">Portuguese inventions</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_Africa" title="Portuguese in Africa">Portuguese in Africa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lusotropicalism" title="Lusotropicalism">Lusotropicalism</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Surinamese" title="Portuguese Surinamese">Portuguese Surinamese</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
